class:
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/mapper/geo/GeoPointFieldMapper.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/query/GeoBoundingBoxFilterParser.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/query/GeoDistanceFilterParser.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/query/GeoDistanceRangeFilterParser.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/query/GeoPolygonFilterParser.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/search/geo/GeoUtils.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/index/search/geo/LatLng.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/search/facet/geodistance/GeoDistanceFacetProcessor.java
modules/elasticsearch/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/search/sort/GeoDistanceSortParser.java
comments:
Geo: Automatically normalize lat/lon on search components, closes #1264.
Glad you fixed the bug on `index.mapper.geo.GeoPointFieldMapper` causing infinite loops for lng = -360-180 = -540 (among other) because of the while test comparison being non strict.
However -180 and 180 can still be returned, they should instead be equal to the same value. Idem for -0.0 and 0.0.
Moreover, this implementation can be **very slow** for huge positive or negative values.

I suggest using Java's floating point modulus operation (see [the JLS](http://java.sun.com/docs/books/jls/third_edition/html/expressions.html#15.17.3))

``` java
// Definition: floatingpointModulusCentered(x,d) = y such as y is in ] -d/2 ; d/2 ] and -0.0 becomes 0.0
// Note that -inf, +inf and NaN will yield NaN
// IMPORTANT: divisor is supposed to be a positive value. (A negative won't mess the modulus but will mess with the rest).
public static double floatingpointModulusCentered(double dividend, double divisor) {
        double rtn = dividend % divisor; // yield a value between 0 and dividend (or -dividend and 0)
        if (rtn <= 0) // get rid of the negative range for the positive one
                rtn += divisor;
        if (rtn > divisor/2) // transform the positive range to a 0-centered one
                rtn -= divisor;
        return rtn;
}
```

I made a [pull request](https://github.com/elasticsearch/elasticsearch/pull/1602) for that.
